### Post by Vorian on 2008-09-30
Rules:
 
1. Forum guidelines on content apply. In other words, safe for kids and safe for work.
2. Try not to quote embedded images; take a moment to snip them out.
3. Off-topic posts will be edited or moved.
4. Thumbnail your image, or use the forum's attachment system. Full-size embedded images are annoying and will be snipped mercilessly.
5. Take a moment and tell everyone the details of your desktop, such as the theme name, the wallpaper name, the icons and any programs you're using in the image.

Enjoy!

---

### Post by sunexplodes on 2008-10-01
> **OmniCloud said:**
> Nice wallpaper...is there anyway, I could get a panel to look like that in Xfce? I love the see-through spaced black look. 


It looks to me like he's using Tint, which is a different panel app. You could easily kill xfce-panel and use tint instead, but you'd also have to use a stand-alone systray app, as tint doesn't have one.

Custom start button using KBFX.

Apps in the first screen are AWN Terminal and Totem (my VLC decided it wanted to bork this morning), and the apps in the other screen are Nautilus, GNOME Do and Google Gadget Sidebar. The desktop globe is Compiz with Cube Atlantis, but I'm not sure why my skydome isn't showing up or my gradient isn't working.

I do have a screenshot showing my Firefox theme, but I didn't want to post a fifth screenshot. I'll post it if anyone wants to see it. ### Post by Barrucadu on 2008-10-01
> **andrek said:**
> **@Barrucadu**, how did you add "pacman" progressbar into arch's pacman? Also, what's the font you're using here in the terminal?

For the progress bar, put "ILoveCandy" in your /etc/pacman.conf, and I'm using "anorexia" (part of the artwiz-fonts package) as my fixed width font.

### Post by BOBSONATOR on 2008-10-02
> **thomasboleyn said:**
> Hi there, amazing looking desk, how did you get the gnome clock to display the full weekday by the way?

Thanks man,

(thanks to What Is In a Name?)

For the clock, open gconf-editor, >> apps >> panel >> applets >> applet n (the one that says Gnome:Clock) >> prefs >> edit custom_format and place "<span color="#F37800">%A, %d %B</span>   %H:%M %Z" you can change the colour and format of course. :popcorn:

---

Changed my desktop a bit. The basic layout is the same old dual panel GNOME arrangement, but the tone is a bit warmer and, I hope, soothing.

[[IMG]http://b.imagehost.org/t/0940/ecra.jpg[/IMG]](http://b.imagehost.org/view/0940/ecra.png) [[IMG]http://b.imagehost.org/t/0319/ecra2.jpg[/IMG]](http://b.imagehost.org/view/0319/ecra2.png) [[IMG]http://b.imagehost.org/t/0277/ecra3.jpg[/IMG]](http://b.imagehost.org/view/0277/ecra3.png)

GTK theme: a modified version of Caramello, made to have dark menus (I still find the hybrid look very fashionable);
Metacity theme: K03, the borderless version, with the background color changed to #2b2b2b;
Icons: Eikon2, as usual;
Fonts: Lucida Sans 7,1pt, except for the windows titles, where I use LucidaMacBold, 7pt;
Wallpaper: one of the many proposals for the Intrepid Ibex release. I got it somewhere here in the forums, but the picture's name is apparently "Red Ibex". If that isn't any help, I can upload it again here in the topic.

And one of my favourite Portuguese bands playing, to help to the peaceful mood. Rádio Macau FTW.

### Post by supersonicdarky on 2008-10-03
> **fedex1993 said:**
> can i get your conky config is super nice :)
here you go
```
background yes
double_buffer yes
use_xft yes

default_shade_color black
default_outline_color white
own_window_transparent yes

#own window to run simultanious 2 or more conkys
own_window yes
own_window_type desktop
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager 

#borders
draw_borders no
border_margin 0

#shades
draw_shades no

#position
gap_x 0
gap_y 0
alignment bottom_left

#behaviour
update_interval 0.5

#colour
default_color  white

#default_shade_color 10335a
#own_window_colour black

#font
use_xft no
xftfont silkscreen:pixelsize=8

#to prevent window from moving
use_spacer no
minimum_size 1680 10

TEXT
$alignc${color 10335a}${time %I:%M %p}$color ${time %A, %b %d %Y} | ${color}Up: ${color 10335a}${uptime_short}${color} | Cpu: ${color 10335a}${cpu}% ${color}${cpugraph 8,30} | ${color }Mem: ${color 10335a}$memperc% ${color}| /: ${color 10335a}${fs_used_perc /}%${color} | /data: ${color 10335a}${fs_used_perc /media/data}%${color} | /ext: ${color 10335a}${fs_used_perc /media/ext}%${color} | Down: ${color 10335a}${downspeed wlan0} ${color}k/s ${downspeedgraph wlan0 8,30} | Up: ${color 10335a}${upspeed wlan0}${color} k/s ${upspeedgraph wlan0 8,30} | Currently ${color 10335a}${execi 600 perl ~/.conky/weather.pl CAXX0343 c w | grep Feels | colrm 1 16 | colrm 3}${color}C, ${color 10335a}${execi 600 perl ~/.conky/weather.pl CAXX0343 c c}
```

---

### Post by kaivalagi on 2008-10-05
> **Truedream said:**
> 
Direction option seems not to be working.

Any issues ask on the conkyForecast thread...

Make sure you use the latest version of the script, the one available for download in the Arch linux forum is well out of date...

Also it is a common misconception that the wind direction arrows point the wrong way. However if the wind direction was NW for example the arrow shouldn't point NW, it should point SE on purpose. The wind is north westerly so comes from that direction, and heads south easterly...

As far as I am aware nothing is broken with the script...

---

### Post by KneeTie on 2008-10-05
> **What is in a name? said:**
> ...And the awesome Conky config everybody is talking about, with some personal tweaks to make it fit on my tiny 1280x800 pixels desktop:

[[img]http://xs132.xs.to/xs132/08400/ecra425.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs132&d=08400&f=ecra425.png) [[img]http://xs232.xs.to/xs232/08400/ecra2520.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs232&d=08400&f=ecra2520.png)


can you post the script you use to launch all the seperate conkys i would like 2 of them not all and would be really cool if i can go by your config and go from there.

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-10-05
> **KneeTie said:**
> can you post the script you use to launch all the seperate conkys i would like 2 of them not all and would be really cool if i can go by your config and go from there.

Sure!

```
#!/bin/bash
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_clock &
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_weather &
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_sys &
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_net &
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_disk &
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_mpd
```

You'll just have to comment out the conky files you don't want to run.

---

### Post by KneeTie on 2008-10-05
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Sure!

```
#!/bin/bash
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_clock &
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_weather &
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_sys &
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_net &
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_disk &
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_mpd
```

You'll just have to comment out the conky files you don't want to run.

thx for the really quick reply , and you sure make desktops look good.

### Post by crimesaucer on 2008-10-08
To get this thread back on topic, check out these RGBA patches for the murrine-svn engine:

[IMG]http://i480.photobucket.com/albums/rr169/Arch-newb/Screenshot-40.png[/IMG]

[http://i480.photobucket.com/albums/rr169/Arch-newb/Screenshot-40-b-1.jpg](http://i480.photobucket.com/albums/rr169/Arch-newb/Screenshot-40-b-1.jpg)
(edited with black background)

There are other apps that have rgba patches, but my Thunar File System would only show as transparent when in the root..... so, I decided to just wait for this to get perfected before I patch my whole system to be transparent.


If Thunar had worked, I would of built Epiphany and used the rgba plugin for that, along with gedit that also had an easy to install plugin that worked good, and my totem-xine that patched, but took a bit of editing.

---

### Post by crimesaucer on 2008-10-08
I'm stoked!!!!!

I found an old patch for the xfce4-panel that I used to work with my gtkrc-2.0 using the murrine-svn engine and rgba = TRUE !!!!!!!


Now I have full opacity for icons and text, as well as murrine buttons.


[IMG]http://i480.photobucket.com/albums/rr169/Arch-newb/Screenshot-41-1.png[/IMG]

Large View: [http://i480.photobucket.com/albums/rr169/Arch-newb/Screenshot-41.png](http://i480.photobucket.com/albums/rr169/Arch-newb/Screenshot-41.png)

---

### Post by andrek on 2008-10-08
> **crimesaucer said:**
> I'm stoked!!!!!

I found an old patch for the xfce4-panel that I used to work with my gtkrc-2.0 using the murrine-svn engine and rgba = TRUE !!!!!!!


Now I have full opacity for icons and text, as well as murrine buttons.


Wow, looks pretty amazing.. You should do a HOW-TO on that!

---

### Post by crimesaucer on 2008-10-08
> **andrek said:**
> Wow, looks pretty amazing.. You should do a HOW-TO on that!

Thanks, but I wouldn't feel good about making a HowTo for this because it took a patch that is pretty old from here: [http://blog.xfce.org/?p=177](http://blog.xfce.org/?p=177)


I remember reading about it last year and thinking that I might like to try this one day..... well after messing around with the RGBA = TRUE in the murrine-svn themes, I decided to try and patch my xfce4-panel..... it worked!  (some plugins were ugly with gray backgrounds)


For more info on the Murrine RGBA check here: [http://www.cimitan.com/blog/2008/04/01/flat-menubars-and-toolbars-for-murrine-rgba-ugly-hack-d/](http://www.cimitan.com/blog/2008/04/01/flat-menubars-and-toolbars-for-murrine-rgba-ugly-hack-d/)

and here for patches/plugins: [http://www.cimitan.com/murrine/rgba-support/list](http://www.cimitan.com/murrine/rgba-support/list)



also really cool:

[http://www.cimitan.com/blog/2007/12/12/gtk-rgba-transparent-widgets-with-the-murrine-engine/](http://www.cimitan.com/blog/2007/12/12/gtk-rgba-transparent-widgets-with-the-murrine-engine/)
[http://www.cimitan.com/blog/2008/02/17/rgba-colormap-by-default-in-gtk-call-for-a-coder/](http://www.cimitan.com/blog/2008/02/17/rgba-colormap-by-default-in-gtk-call-for-a-coder/)

### Post by crimesaucer on 2008-10-08
> **Cimi86 said:**
> ".....You should enable the blur for **every windows** not just the decorations!!! Your shots look still ugly to me :)....."

Ouch..... but I see what you mean.


When I enabled the Terminal to use blur, it made it's smoothness look a lot better..... sort of like your smooth themes:

[IMG]http://i480.photobucket.com/albums/rr169/Arch-newb/Screenshot-47-1.png[/IMG]

Large View: [http://i480.photobucket.com/albums/rr169/Arch-newb/Screenshot-47-2.jpg](http://i480.photobucket.com/albums/rr169/Arch-newb/Screenshot-47-2.jpg)


Anyway, I would have the entire theme like this if I could, but the 3rd party xfce4 rgba patch for Thunar would only show when in "gksu thunar", and not the regular way. 


Gedit looked good with the plugin, and so did Totem-xine, but if I can't have Firefox and Thunar, then I'll wait for people to perfect it for xfce4 and firefox.


This is basically all I have to change to make it smooth when that happens (uncomment and gradient 2)

```

#GtkToolbar              ::shadow-type          = GTK_SHADOW_NONE  # Makes toolbars flat and unified.
#GtkMenuBar              ::shadow_type          = GTK_SHADOW_NONE

``` 

and this:

```


menubarstyle        = 1     # 0 = flat, 1 = glassy, 2 = gradient, 3 = striped
toolbarstyle	    = 1     # 0 = flat, 1 = glassy, 2 = gradient

```


..... but your tip did help my xfce4-panel..... it won't work with both xfce4-panel and the Terminal.... so I chose the panel app:

[IMG]http://i480.photobucket.com/albums/rr169/Arch-newb/Screenshot-46.png[/IMG]

Large View: [http://i480.photobucket.com/albums/rr169/Arch-newb/Screenshot-46-1.jpg](http://i480.photobucket.com/albums/rr169/Arch-newb/Screenshot-46-1.jpg)



..... I'm done spamming now.

### Post by crimesaucer on 2008-10-08
> **cardinals_fan said:**
> @crimesaucer: I'm not a fan of your theme

I'm sorry to hear that. I though it was one of my best so far (for a beginner them maker).

> "..... but the way you integrated the colors on your desktop to match with the autumn leaves background is impressive.


I actually made the emerald window theme first, using the vista buttons from an old beryl theme. I remade the buttons to always have the red button show, and the glass effect even on the in-active windows..... 


Then the look that I was trying to match with the gtk was the red vista button, and the clear vista button. 


Then I made the Murrine theme using the glossy/beryl style, and made it to match the emerald theme I made..... and I was trying to not have a gray or silver gtk, but rather a milky white look.


Then I found the perfect autumn wallpaper that matched the White, Red, and Black color palette.


After that I used the xfce4-panel patch/hack, and lastly the blur fix from Cimi.

---

KDE:  Serenity with Ecstatic global style.

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-10-09

### Post by isecore on 2008-10-09
GTK/Metacity is called Mira, can be [found on Gnome-Look]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Mira?content=89831"). It really needs the Artwiz fonts to look the best. 

Wallpaper is Eternal War by Ladyrapid, can [be found here]("http://ladyrapid.deviantart.com/art/E-t-e-r-n-a-l-W-a-r-81415905"). Icon theme is good old UbuntuStudio, available in the repos. I have yet to find a nicer icon-theme that is SVG-scalable. 

Y'all can click on the image for a full-size version with some minor censorship :)

[[IMG]http://gallery.isecore.net/cache/computer-stuff/screenshot_2008-10-09_nojunk.png_595.jpg[/IMG]]("http://gallery.isecore.net/albums/computer-stuff/screenshot_2008-10-09_nojunk.png")

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-10-10
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> my first thought was "why can't we all just get along?" that's pretty sharp looking. best i've ever seen xp look.
Kind of like Giant Speck's sig :D

Also, my / partition is JFS (apparently it's nearly impossible to install GRUB on XFS, which I used for my other partitions). So far, it seems really slow. It takes about 14 seconds for /usr/bin to load in Thunar. On Reiser3, it took about half that long. The only reason I didn't keep using Reiser was that it really slows down the boot time. On my next install I might go back to Reiser, since I would rather have a fast filesystem than a fast boot (my computer is usually on for days at a time, so what's a few extra seconds at boot every week or so?).

### Post by hellion0 on 2008-10-10
Ok... again I must buck the trend with October. Actually, this desktop is kind of modeled off of some of the Xubuntu Intrepid mockups.

[[IMG]http://img231.imageshack.us/img231/7855/gardevoiroct08iz5.th.png[/IMG]](http://img231.imageshack.us/my.php?image=gardevoiroct08iz5.png)

Wallpaper: [Neutron Revolver](http://interfacelift.com/wallpaper_beta/details/1018/neutron_revolver.html)
GTK: [Blue-Joy](http://www.xfce-look.org/content/show.php/Blue+Joy?content=73387)
XFCE: Symphony (Seriously, do you expect me to use anything else at this point?)
Icons: [Oxygen-Refit2](http://download.tuxfamily.org/oxygenrefit/OxygenRefit2-2.2.0.tar.bz2) (Link is a direct download)
XMMS: [xmms-darkness](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/xmms-darkness?content=70763)
Fonts: Titlebar and Conky use MiscFixed, everything else uses Segoe UI

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-10-10

But yes, I like your concept a lot, as I said.

### Post by Truedream on 2008-10-11
Go to this thread. [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=205865](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=205865)


After that you'll need to edit the files in the  screenshot according to your prefrences and create a small starting script for them i.e.

```
#!/bin/bash

sleep 25 &&
conky -d -c ~/.conky/Mira_green/.conkyrc_clock &
sleep 25 &&
conky -d -c ~/.conky/Mira_green/.conkyrc_weather &
sleep 25 &&
conky -d -c ~/.conky/Mira_green/.conkyrc_sys &
sleep 25 &&
conky -d -c ~/.conky/Mira_green/.conkyrc_net &
sleep 25 &&
conky -d -c ~/.conky/Mira_green/.conkyrc_disk &
sleep 25 &&
conky -d -c ~/.conky/Mira_green/.conkyrc_mpd &
exit

```


[[IMG]http://img372.imageshack.us/img372/2710/screenshotcf9.th.png[/IMG]](http://img372.imageshack.us/my.php?image=screenshotcf9.png)[[IMG]http://img372.imageshack.us/images/thpix.gif[/IMG]](http://g.imageshack.us/thpix.php)

---

### Post by Killeroid on 2008-10-12
[[IMG]http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3228/2933033665_39e2e9ec2a.jpg[/IMG]](http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3228/2933033665_05099448d1_o.png)

[[IMG]http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3285/2933033529_c620654bea.jpg[/IMG]](http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3285/2933033529_a9555d0057_o.png)

Using tint for my taskbar and trayer for notification area. 

Metacity: [**Magnum (Minimal Scrollbars)**](http://fratrip.deviantart.com/art/Magnum-Suite-84559205)
GTK: [**Tigris**](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Tigris?content=75276)
Icons : [**All Black**](http://mandarancio.deviantart.com/art/ALLBLACK-0-4-70641172)
Wallpaper: **[Pink, Black and Blue](http://nxxos.deviantart.com/art/Black-Pink-and-Blue-Wallpaper-99960557)**
Font: **Calibri 8**

My .tintrc: 
```

#---------------------------------------------
# TINT CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_show_all_desktop = 0
panel_monitor = 1
panel_position = bottom left
panel_size = 1100 22
panel_margin = 1 4
panel_padding = 0 0
font_shadow = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
panel_rounded = 6
panel_border_width = 2
panel_background_color = #F0F0F0 100
panel_border_color = #FFFFFF 100

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 140
task_margin = 2
task_padding = 20
task_icon_size = 0
task_font = Segoe UI 7
task_font_color = #000000 50
task_active_font_color = #ffffff 100

#---------------------------------------------
# TASK BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
task_rounded =5
task_background_color = #000000 0
task_active_background_color = #eeab29 100
task_border_width = 2
task_border_color = #ffffff 0
task_active_border_color = #ffffff 100

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
time1_format =%I:%M
time1_font = advent bold 10
#time2_format = %g.%d.%y
time2_font = Segue UI 6
clock_font_color = #000000 100

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = none
mouse_right = none
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify


```

---

### Post by perfectska04@hotmail.com on 2008-10-12
Hey guys, I came up with a simple, graphical way to completely theme any Ubuntu GNOME desktop in less than 5 minutes (Icons/GDM's/GTK's/Wallpapers). It's specially helpful with new installations or for getting friends to see that linux can be attractive too.

Since many people in these desktop threads use my themes and icons, or simply love customizing their desktops, I thought I'd let you guys play with this app before I submit it to gnome-look or somewhere else.

It's pretty straightforward. You click install, choose your favorite color, and the script grabs the very latest Shiki-Colors GTK's/Gnome-Colors icons/Arc-Colors GDM's and wallpapers and applies them. It even detects wether you have emerald running and applies it (if you do have it running) and checks for your monitor's aspect ratio and applies the GDM's/Wallpapers accordingly.

After installing, there will be three new menu-items. One will let you upgrade the theme, another will let you change the color-scheme quickly, and the third one will let you uninstall everything the script installed.

Feel free to edit it or use it to deploy your own themes.

Read the included README and  install the included Murrine SVN engine .debs if you're not using Intrepid, or you haven't installed Murrine SVN in hardy yet. Hope you guys enjoy it!

Get it here: [http://www.mediafire.com/download.php?eyymgtyk0tc]("http://www.mediafire.com/download.php?eyymgtyk0tc")

---

### Post by Truedream on 2008-10-12
seems to be working just fine for me. Downloaded all the theme/icons etc. and was able to modify it easily. Would be cool if somebody made an app just like Synaptic manager for themes ;)

---

### Post by perfectska04@hotmail.com on 2008-10-12
> **Truedream said:**
> seems to be working just fine for me. Downloaded all the theme/icons etc. and was able to modify it easily. Would be cool if somebody made an app just like Synaptic manager for themes ;)

I think there is a project like that called "Epidermis". They have their own launchpad page, but last time I checked it was still in it's early stages and quite buggy.

Oh, I forgot to mention. The changed GDM's only update after a reboot or gdm reload, since the update feature is still not implemented in GDM.

### Post by perfectska04@hotmail.com on 2008-10-12
> **ayoli said:**
> Interesting.
Did you do that with bash+zenity ?

edit : there is also the gnome splash that you can change (maybe it already can do it, I didn't test)

Yes, I took my previous work on ColorizeMe scripts and spent some time in the man pages for zenity until I figured out how to make the basic GUI. The code is probably not the most optimal by any account (since I'm not really a scripter), but i've tested most of it extensively and worst-case scenario it won't harm anything and can be easily removed. I think for now all that's left is to simplify everything (I'm sure the code can be cut in half) and add support for clearlooks/murrine-colors and Usplash. I don't think I'll bother with gnome-splash, since that is already deprecated and won't be around in the following GNOME releases.

This is mostly an amateur effort to get people who aren't too technically savvy to be able to have some choice other than brown in their Ubuntu desktop.

### Post by Sponzenbroekske on 2008-10-12
> **Zachx65 said:**
> 
I'm going to remove the Gnome panel and was wondering if I need to install a shutdown screenlet, or if using Ctrl+Alt+Backspace is safe.

Maybe YAKUAKE is something for you , actually for every linux-user, its just awesome, dropdownterminal, just make it load at startup.

install
```
sudo apt-get install yakuake
```
then go to sessions and put it in there with the commandname yakuake.

EDIT: ow yeah; the reason why YOU should install install it: press the button (standard F12) there comes the terminal, type sudo reboot or sudo shutdown and then you don't need a widget to do that. You can use the terminal for everything, offcourse, like typing firefox will open firefox (duh!)

> **Zachx65 said:**
> 
Where should I go to make Nautilus look more appealing?

Maybe an alternative, Dolphin is attractive and usefull, but krusader is high appreciated, and also usefull in local networks.

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-10-12
> **Zachx65 said:**
> Here's what I've got ATM. I'd like to finish it off with the screenlets seen in Truedream, and Octagonal's screens. I particularly like the weather and email part. Any info on that one guys? 

I'm going to remove the Gnome panel and was wondering if I need to install a shutdown screenlet, or if using Ctrl+Alt+Backspace is safe.

Where should I go to make Nautilus look more appealing?
I think it would be fine to use Ctrl+Alt+Backspace and then shutdown from GDM. Alternatively, you can shutdown your machine with:
```

sudo shutdown -h now

```
And you can reboot with:
```

sudo shutdown -r now

```

I think there may even be a way to logout from Gnome through the command line. As for other actions like suspend and hibernate, I'm not sure.

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-10-13
> **71CH said:**
> Looks great.  How do I modify the weather script for conky?  I couldn't figure it out.

What exactly do you need to know? Is it the location code issue?
If so, it also took me a while to figure it out. Then I realised that I needed to insert the code in every sentence of the .conkyrc_weather file that called the weather script, replacing YourLocation. Like, for instance, this example:

```
${color a4a4a4}${alignc}${execi 3600 python ~/.scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=POXX0020 --datatype=CC}
```

Being POXX0020 my location's code. Repeat the same procedure all the way down the TEXT section of the conky file.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-10-14
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Meanwhile I'm trying to find a new place for Conky on my screen.
If you're trying to maintain the traditional Xfce layout, replace one panel or the other with conky. Either delete the top panel and have conky really skinny and span the full width of the screen or delete the bottom one and let it spread out vertically a bit.

There's also a 3rd option: Like the first way of doing it, just don't delete the top panel ...I think a screenshot would better explain it:

[[IMG]http://img183.imageshack.us/img183/9866/layoutsj5.th.png[/IMG]](http://img183.imageshack.us/my.php?image=layoutsj5.png)[[IMG]http://img183.imageshack.us/images/thpix.gif[/IMG]](http://g.imageshack.us/thpix.php)

This way you could keep both panels and Xfce should still look relatively Xfce-like.

### Post by Ub1476 on 2008-10-14
> **What is in a name? said:**
> A friend of mine is using Intrepid Beta and is experiencing this same issue with Eikon2. The folder icons at the Places menu revert to a very ugly default. Does anybody know if GNOME 2.24 messed around with the names of the icons again? If so, what in the world are the folders icons supposed to be called now?

Not quite sure, but this is from perfectska04:

> Ok, since there is a bug in gnome-icon theme for GNOME 2.24 I will now post a workaround to fix all the issues with icons that inherit from gnome-icon-theme.

type in a terminal and logout afterwards:
sudo rm /usr/share/icons/gnome/scalable/places/inode-directory.svg
sudo rm /usr/share/icons/gnome/32x32/places/inode-directory.png
sudo rm /usr/share/icons/gnome/24x24/places/inode-directory.png
sudo rm /usr/share/icons/gnome/22x22/places/inode-directory.png
sudo rm /usr/share/icons/gnome/16x16/places/inode-directory.png

There, now the bugs discussed a page back will be fixed in GNOME 2.24 (and not only for my themes, but for all other icon themes that inherit icons from gnome)

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-10-14
Yeah compiz and xfce4 are fine together. The only shortcoming is, at the moment, there's no, "window decorator", mode for xfwm4, meaning you need to install emerald as well.

Edit: Should also point out that Xfwm4 supports xcompmgr for much simpler, non-accelerated compositing support. I've got compiz and xcompmgr and I just use xcompmgr.

### Post by perfectska04@hotmail.com on 2008-10-14
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Now, I wonder... If I remove the gnome-icon-theme from the inherits line of Eikon's index.theme file, and reduce it to "Tango,hicolor", will we still have that problem, even if we don't delete the inode-directory icons?

I think that as long as inode-directory icons are installed, there will be many regressions with any icon set (since everything will eventually inherit from gnome). I already submitted a bug to Ubuntu and commented on the bugzilla version, but no one has done anything about it. Anyway, here's a slightly more complete workaround than the one Ub1476 posted:

#This part removes the problem (useless) icons.
sudo rm -f /usr/share/icons/gnome/scalable/places/inode-directory.svg
sudo rm -f /usr/share/icons/gnome/32x32/places/inode-directory.png
sudo rm -f /usr/share/icons/gnome/24x24/places/inode-directory.png
sudo rm -f /usr/share/icons/gnome/22x22/places/inode-directory.png
sudo rm -f /usr/share/icons/gnome/16x16/places/inode-directory.png

#Log out. If for some reason the icons appear as blank after logging out, rebuild gnome-icon-theme's icon cache:
sudo rm -f /usr/share/icons/gnome/icon-theme.cache
sudo gtk-update-icon-cache -qf /usr/share/icons/gnome

---

### Post by lswest on 2008-10-14
> **What is in a name? said:**
> A friend of mine is using Intrepid Beta and is experiencing this same issue with Eikon2. The folder icons at the Places menu revert to a very ugly default. Does anybody know if GNOME 2.24 messed around with the names of the icons again? If so, what in the world are the folders icons supposed to be called now?

I made symbolic links to the folder.png/folder.svg files in the theme called gtk-directory.svg and inode-directory.svg (new names for those).  That solved it for me.

Commands:
```
ln -s ~/.icons/[themename]/scalable/folders.svg ~/.icons/[themename]/scalable/gtk-directory.svg
ln -s ~/.icons/[themename]/scalable/folders.svg ~/.icons/[themename]/scalable/inode-directory.svg
```

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-10-14
> **lswest said:**

Commands:
```
ln -s ~/.icons/[themename]/scalable/folders.svg ~/.icons/[themename]/scalable/gtk-directory.svg
ln -s ~/.icons/[themename]/scalable/folders.svg ~/.icons/[themename]/scalable/inode-directory.svg
```

Yes, I thought of doing that too. Still, Perfectska04 mentioned on that specific thread about that subject that the inode-directory icon has the tendency of overriding any other folder icon, in situations where folder-open or directory-visiting-whatever would be used instead. ### Post by perfectska04@hotmail.com on 2008-10-14
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Yes, I thought of doing that too. Still, Perfectska04 mentioned on that specific thread about that subject that the inode-directory icon has the tendency of overriding any other folder icon, in situations where folder-open or directory-visiting-whatever would be used instead. Do you have the same issue now with those links?

I'm still on Hardy, and won't upgrade to Intrepid until it reaches the RC stage, at least, so I can't test any of this myself, but I'm worried about this.

Yes, if you just add inode-directory to your themes it will fix the folders in the places menu, but it will break many, many things. Besides that does not solve the issue since we can't force every icon theme on the internet to add that ugly workaround just to conform to this bug.

I recommend anyone who can to visit the bug pages and let them know this is important to you and should be fixed:
[http://bugzilla.gnome.org/show_bug.cgi?id=539286](http://bugzilla.gnome.org/show_bug.cgi?id=539286)
[https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/gnome-icon-theme/+bug/278033](https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/gnome-icon-theme/+bug/278033)

### Post by perfectska04@hotmail.com on 2008-10-14
> **lswest said:**
> I haven't noticed any other errors regarding folders, that link fixes the places menu and I haven't noticed any other issues.

Try drag n' dropping a file into a folder. The folder won't change to an 'open folder'. Also, in nautilus' non-browser mode, visiting folders will appear as closed folders. In many other cases, home-folder or other random icons will simply be forced to look like a closed folder. This is why the link is not a true fix. The only fix is to remove inode-directory or let the GNOME team know that they should go back to how it used to be in previous versions. inode-directory.icon is harmless and was included before, but inode-directory.png/svg was never included until recently and this is why these issues started happening.

---

### Post by perfectska04@hotmail.com on 2008-10-14

Hey, What is in a name?, I just recently installed conky (and I've no idea how to customize it yet). What would I have to do to make it look just like in the pictures you posted?

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-10-14
> **perfectska04@hotmail.com said:**
> Hey, What is in a name?, I just recently installed conky (and I've no idea how to customize it yet). What would I have to do to make it look just like in the pictures you posted?

Hi! 
I basically downloaded a set with conkyrc files and scripts someone else provided at the ArchLinux forums and also here at this thread. I uploaded a slightly modded version of those to drop.io, just because I don't have an NVidia card (the original scripts measured those), I use Ubuntu, so I don't need a Pacman status script (the original config had one), etc. If you download those, place the two folders, .scripts and .conky, right inside of your home folder.

Then, to launch all of those conkyrc files at once, it's recommended to create a bash script which launches all of them, and to save it on your $PATH (I just placed it on /usr/local/bin). Like this script I just called conky_start:

```
#!/bin/bash
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_clock &
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_weather &
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_sys &
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_net &
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_disk &
conky -c ~/.conky/Mira_multi/.conkyrc_mpd
```

Save it, make it executable, and you should be done. Run the command conky_start to make it work. If you have any other question, just ask.

---

### Post by cookieofdoom on 2008-10-14
> **What is in a name? said:**
> What exactly do you need to know? Is it the location code issue?
If so, it also took me a while to figure it out. Then I realised that I needed to insert the code in every sentence of the .conkyrc_weather file that called the weather script, replacing YourLocation. Like, for instance, this example:

```
${color a4a4a4}${alignc}${execi 3600 python ~/.scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=POXX0020 --datatype=CC}
```

Being POXX0020 my location's code. Repeat the same procedure all the way down the TEXT section of the conky file.

Right now I'm using Tint2 as my task bar, so I only really need to get it working with my system tray. Although I can't seem to get the color changed anywhere.

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-10-14
> **cookieofdoom said:**
> Great desktop. I'm trying to setup xfce on my laptop, but I can't figure out how you got your panels to be black (or dark gray). I've tried all the guides, but none of them seem to be working. Right now I'm using Tint2 as my task bar, so I only really need to get it working with my system tray. Although I can't seem to get the color changed anywhere.

Thanks for all your help in this thread! I've learned quite a bit from your posts.

Well, I have to thank you too for your compliments!

I realise that trying to change the colour of the Xfce4-panel alone is not the easiest task. In my case, I just use already existing GTK themes which have dark panels. That's the basic point. Now, some of them, like the ones I've been using lately, aren't exactly "Xfce-ready" at the origin, because, while they theme the GNOME panel to appear with a dark tone, they don't apply the same settings to the Xfce panel. So I just changed a bit some of the code at the gtkrc files of those themes, in order to solve that issue. You can grab some of those themes from my drop.io page (check my signature). It's a piece of code at the final sections of the file (those when we associate styles with GTK widgets), and it has been working with all themes I came across, so far.

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-10-15

That is freaking awesome.  I downloaded the Emerald theme and color scheme and made slight tweaks to both and then I set up gtk-qt-engine to theme all my GTK apps with the Dust theme.

Let's take a look, shall we?

1. Here we have Firefox, using the Dust Firefox theme.  Google appears dark because of a Firefox add-on called Stylish, as I've said a few times already.  And of course, there is Pandora, which is currently darkened because of Compiz's handy "ADD Helper" plugin.

[[IMG]http://i279.photobucket.com/albums/kk122/SpecKtacle/th_dustomino.png[/IMG]](http://i279.photobucket.com/albums/kk122/SpecKtacle/dustomino.png)

[[IMG]http://i279.photobucket.com/albums/kk122/SpecKtacle/th_dustomino3.png[/IMG]](http://i279.photobucket.com/albums/kk122/SpecKtacle/dustomino3.png)

4. Here is a look at my desktop.  The wallpaper is called intelmac-orange and is available from deviantART.  The dock on the left is cairo-dock, with custom dock icons fashioned out of a window icon I found in the Snowish icon theme.  The panel on the right is just an ordinary panel with shortcuts to my major folders, such as Documents and Pictures.  The start menu is a modification I made to a button I found a long time ago.  And finally, the panel applet on the top is Knewsticker, set to 55% transparency with Compiz.

### Post by cookieofdoom on 2008-10-15
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Well, I have to thank you too for your compliments!

I realise that trying to change the colour of the Xfce4-panel alone is not the easiest task. In my case, I just use already existing GTK themes which have dark panels. That's the basic point. Now, some of them, like the ones I've been using lately, aren't exactly "Xfce-ready" at the origin, because, while they theme the GNOME panel to appear with a dark tone, they don't apply the same settings to the Xfce panel. So I just changed a bit some of the code at the gtkrc files of those themes, in order to solve that issue. You can grab some of those themes from my drop.io page (check my signature). It's a piece of code at the final sections of the file (those when we associate styles with GTK widgets), and it has been working with all themes I came across, so far.

____________________________________________________

Slowly modding Ciano to have a smoother look. I also went back to that Niva wallpaper I love:

[[img]http://xs232.xs.to/xs232/08422/ecrablue302.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs232&d=08422&f=ecrablue302.png)

That bit of code about "Panel" is exactly what I was looking for! I just modified Dust (the Ubuntu GTK theme) and now I have a dark panel. Thanks so much for your help! I'll be uploading a screenshot once I finish getting everything worked out. :guitar:

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-10-15
> **cookieofdoom said:**
> Great desktop. I'm trying to setup xfce on my laptop, but I can't figure out how you got your panels to be black (or dark gray). I've tried all the guides, but none of them seem to be working. Right now I'm using Tint2 as my task bar, so I only really need to get it working with my system tray. Although I can't seem to get the color changed anywhere.

Thanks for all your help in this thread! I've learned quite a bit from your posts.

Add the following to your ~/.gtkrc-2.0 file:

```
style "panel"
{
font_name="Dungeon 7"
bg[NORMAL] = "#2d2d2d"
bg_pixmap[NORMAL] = "background.png" # place background.png in your ~/ dir or add full path
fg[NORMAL] = "#bfbfbf" # this affects all normal text
text[NORMAL] = "#bfbfbf" # this affects clock text
}

widget_class "*Panel*" style "panel"
widget "*Panel*" style "panel"
class "*Panel*" style "panel"
```

Change it as applicable.



Also, looking good, Wiian. Just don't use an OSX-style GTK+ theme. At this point, it would be tragic. :p

Edit: Also, something I forgot to check when I tried all those menus. In total, how much memory are all those xfce4-menu-plugins using? I've only got one currently and it's using 5mb.

### Post by eightmillion on 2008-10-15
> **Giant Speck said:**
> That is freaking awesome.  I downloaded the Emerald theme and color scheme and made slight tweaks to both and then I set up gtk-qt-engine to theme all my GTK apps with the Dust theme.


That's great. :) I learned the other day that you can't set your gtk apps to use your qt theme and at the same time set your qt apps to use your gtk theme. It's like dividing by zero. Everything crashes. :lolflag:
> **Daisuke_Aramaki said:**
> thanx mate! btw, ne details on ur icon set, both in this screen and ur previous screens? :):)
The icons in both shots are [Oxygen Refit 2 Black]("http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/Oxygen+Refit+Black?content=89298"). I just change the folder icons periodically. I have a script that changes them all at once. Here it is...
```
#!/bin/bash
convert -geometry 128x128 -sharpen 0x.4 $1 ./128x128/places/$2
convert -geometry 64x64 -sharpen 0x.4 $1 ./64x64/places/$2
convert -geometry 48x48 -sharpen 0x.4 $1 ./48x48/places/$2
convert -geometry 32x32 -sharpen 0x.4 $1 ./32x32/places/$2
convert -geometry 22x22 -sharpen 0x.4 $1 ./22x22/places/$2
convert -geometry 16x16 -sharpen 0x.4 $1 ./16x16/places/$2
exit 0

```
Save the script as something like places and make it executable and then drop it and your folder icon in the root directory of the icon theme you are wanting to change and run this script like this. ./places genericfolder.png folder.png

The first argument is the input file and the second is the icon in the theme you are trying to change. You may want to make a backup of the original icon. Just copy ~/.kde/share/icons/NAMEOFICONTHEME/places/128x128/folder.png somewhere else for safe keeping.

> **Daisuke_Aramaki said:**
> hope it aint too much to ask, is a domino config in the pipeline? :guitar:

I see that Giant Speck took care of you. I've just been using the attached domino config. I've tried to make it as oxygen like as possible so that Amarok 1.4 fits in better with KDE 4.

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2008-10-15
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> LOL!1 me too.

Turns out I'm a liar anyway. I figured out the icons thing. If the name specified in the index.theme file isn't the same as the folder, the thing doesn't work. Hence "Eikon" and "Meliae" worked, but "GNOME-Brave" and "hydroxygen" didn't.

### Post by perfectska04@hotmail.com on 2008-10-15
> **Giant Speck said:**
> I know how to do [COLOR="RoyalBlue"]**_this_**[/COLOR], but how do you do [COLOR="Red"]**_this_**[/COLOR]?

As far as I know, you can make QT4 apps use your native GTK theme by installing "qgtkstyle". I also installed qt4-qtconfig to set it up.

I use the following repo in Ubuntu Hardy:
deb [http://ppa.launchpad.net/martin-espinoza/ubuntu](http://ppa.launchpad.net/martin-espinoza/ubuntu) hardy main
deb-src [http://ppa.launchpad.net/martin-espinoza/ubuntu](http://ppa.launchpad.net/martin-espinoza/ubuntu) hardy main

I've attached a picture of Virtualbox 2.0.2 using GTK. /offtopic

### Post by tenderone on 2008-10-16
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Well, I have to thank you too for your compliments!

I realise that trying to change the colour of the Xfce4-panel alone is not the easiest task. In my case, I just use already existing GTK themes which have dark panels. That's the basic point. Now, some of them, like the ones I've been using lately, aren't exactly "Xfce-ready" at the origin, because, while they theme the GNOME panel to appear with a dark tone, they don't apply the same settings to the Xfce panel. So I just changed a bit some of the code at the gtkrc files of those themes, in order to solve that issue. You can grab some of those themes from my drop.io page (check my signature). It's a piece of code at the final sections of the file (those when we associate styles with GTK widgets), and it has been working with all themes I came across, so far.

### Post by urukrama on 2008-10-17
> **SomeGuyDude said:**
> My thing is that I use a lot of alt-tabbing, keeping my windows arranged so I can see just enough of each one that if there's activity I switch to it. The idea of my windows each taking up a quarter of the screen strikes me as hard to get used to (especially in the case of web pages). But I'm always willing to learn.

That was how I thought before I ventured into the land of tiling window managers. I now regularly use Awesome, and find it very useful, especially on older machines where I use a lot of light command-line applications. If you use it properly, the tags system is very handy to keep you focussed and keep your windows organised.

I don't do much tiling, though. I generally have about 5 tags/workspaces, and only one of them is set to tile by default, and I only use command-line applications on that tag; two tags are floating, two are maximized. The option to tile, though, is good to have around. It allows you to see what you have running in that tag, and can be really useful when you have to compare two documents.

I still use Openbox as well, but once you get used to them, tiling window managers are handy.

---

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2008-10-17
> **urukrama said:**
> I don't do much tiling, though. I generally have about 5 tags/workspaces, and only one of them is set to tile by default, and I only use command-line applications on that tag; two tags are floating, two are maximized. The option to tile, though, is good to have around. It allows you to see what you have running in that tag, and can be really useful when you have to compare two documents.

I still use Openbox as well, but once you get used to them, tiling window managers are handy.

why not just maximize a terminal on one workspace in openbox and tile it with dvtm, or a combination of screen and dvtm, then use the rest of the workspaces as you normally would in openbox? i went through a mad tiling period, but i found i don't type well enough to take full advantage of tiling. i'm a lot faster with a mouse.

Oh. My. Goodness.
**I'm in love with Murrina334.** Dbbolton, you did a terrific job, it's wonderful!!!

Here are some screenshots with it. I just changed both the x and ythickness values on the "panel" style to 2, in order to give the impression that all the icons on the bottom panel have the same padding and height (I'm mixing task icons with launchers, the trash widget... They all seem to have different sizes on Xfce, depending on how you work the panel around).

Still looking for the perfect wallpaper, but Duality Wide looks cool to me: [http://osox.deviantart.com/art/Duality-Wide-77149850](http://osox.deviantart.com/art/Duality-Wide-77149850)

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-10-18
> **ad_267 said:**
> Yeah doesn't work for me either. Does this require a more recent version of the Murrine engine than the one in Intrepid?

I don't want to be nosey, but... 
Probably it will be helpful to apply Murrina334 and then run an app through the terminal. It should print some errors referring to the gtkrc if it's not working. If so, copy them and post them on this topic. Murrina SVN has been changed a lot recently, so yeah, unfortunately it's a hassle for all of us who develop themes with it and try to make our work compatible with as many users as possible.

---

### Post by ad_267 on 2008-10-18
I get this:

```
/home/adam/.themes/Murrina334/gtk-2.0/gtkrc:83: error: unexpected identifier `profile', expected character `}'
```

---

### Post by cookieofdoom on 2008-10-18
> **What is in a name? said:**
> I don't want to be nosey, but... 
Probably it will be helpful to apply Murrina334 and then run an app through the terminal. It should print some errors referring to the gtkrc if it's not working. If so, copy them and post them on this topic. Murrina SVN has been changed a lot recently, so yeah, unfortunately it's a hassle for all of us who develop themes with it and try to make our work compatible with as many users as possible.

Good idea... I got what ad_267 got... only with my name as the home directory. I'm trying to tweak it... I'll post if I get anything.

EDIT: Fixed it. On line 83 of the gtkrc file, replace "profile" with "style". It should work just fine. :)

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-10-18
I guess Intrepid still has a less-than-new version of Murrina. A few revisions ago, Murrina SVN allowed for the use of the word "style" where "profile" is now used. If Intrepid's Murrina can't recognize the expression "profile", try to replace it with "style" and then reapply the theme.

EDIT: Yes, cookieofdoom. Exactly. You got it first. ;)

---

### Post by ad_267 on 2008-10-18
Thanks, that worked.

> I guess Intrepid still has a less-than-new version of Murrina. A few revisions ago, Murrina SVN allowed for the use of the word "style" where "profile" is now used. If Intrepid's Murrina can't recognize the expression "profile", try to replace it with "style" and then reapply the theme.

Some people on gnome-look complained that my newer Murrine themes didn't work with the SVN version of the engine, even though I explicitly stated that they were for 0.60 .

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2008-10-19
> **SomeGuyDude said:**
> Here's a question for you all: which piece of the theme is your "base"?

Meaning, when you build the theme, which part do you start with? Do you find a great wallpaper and decide what goes on that, or does a GTK or icon theme strike your fancy and things have to fit that?

for me, it can start anywhere. it's a lot easier to find a wallpaper that fits a gtk theme than the other way around, so i use gtk themes that are easily adapted (elegant brit, nova, etc). as i've been using opera lately, i've noticed that some of the newer skins are more easily matched up with gtk themes.

two new screenshots...

dwm
[[IMG]http://d.imagehost.org/t/0953/dwmscr.jpg[/IMG]](http://d.imagehost.org/view/0953/dwmscr.jpg)

i edited the config file to match the colors in dwm to the ones i picked for xterm.


openbox
[[IMG]http://d.imagehost.org/t/0373/mookscr.jpg[/IMG]](http://d.imagehost.org/view/0373/mookscr.jpg)

this is a case where an opera skin matched pretty well to the gtk theme (mookid).

### Post by crimesaucer on 2008-10-19
> **leafdog said:**
> A question, Can a newer version of an engine (Murrine) alter or/and improve the same theme?

All of my old murrine themes that I made, improved a bit when I installed the murrine-svn engine.


The themes basically stayed the same, except for the tabs looked much better with the new glossy tabs.


Plus, you can now add some of the new settings into your old gtkrc and make them look much better with the new murrine-svn engine. You could even add rgba transparency or nice gradients like the dust and smooth themes.

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-10-20
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Hey, I don't even have to build it from source this time.

Meanwhile, if you want to have something more recent and use Subversion, checkout from here:

```
svn checkout http://svn.gnome.org/svn/murrine/trunk/ murrine
```

and then:

```
cd murrine
./autogen.sh --prefix=/usr --enable-animation
make
sudo make install

```

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-10-20
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Meanwhile... Is anybody having this same problem with Tahoma and Firefox? If so, any idea why? I've been trying to google this issue for months, but no go so far.

[[img]http://xs132.xs.to/xs132/08431/madtahoma409.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs132&d=08431&f=madtahoma409.png) [[img]http://xs132.xs.to/xs132/08431/madtahoma2162.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs132&d=08431&f=madtahoma2162.png)

Try running these commands in the terminal, and then restart the X-server:

```
sudo dpkg-reconfigure fontconfig-config
sudo dpkg-reconfigure fontconfig
```

That used to happen to me a lot, and these font reconfigurations usually help.

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-10-20

sudo dpkg-reconfigure fontconfig-config
sudo dpkg-reconfigure fontconfig
```

# set to yes if you want Conky to be forked in the background
background yes

cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 2

out_to_console no

# X font when Xft is disabled, you can pick one with program xfontsel
#font 7x12
#font 6x10
#font 7x13
#font 8x13
#font 7x12
#font *mintsmild.se*
#font -*-*-*-*-*-*-34-*-*-*-*-*-*-*
#font -artwiz-snap-normal-r-normal-*-*-100-*-*-p-*-iso8859-1

# Use Xft?
use_xft yes

# Xft font when Xft is enabled
xftfont Zekton:size=9

# Text alpha when using Xft
xftalpha 1

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# mail spool
mail_spool $MAIL

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 1

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
own_window_type override

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 200 5
maximum_width 400

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw outlines?

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders no

# border margins
border_margin 4

# border width
border_width 10

# Default colors and also border colors
default_color white
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color DarkGrey
color1 white #00FF00
color2 white #EEAA00
color3 white #9933FF

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
#alignment top_left
#alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
alignment bottom_right

# Gap between borders of screen and text
gap_x 10
gap_y 10

# Add spaces to keep things from moving about?  This only affects certain objects.
use_spacer right

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase no

# none, xmms, bmp, audacious, infopipe (default is none)


# boinc (seti) dir
# seti_dir /opt/seti

# Possible variables to be used:
#
#  Variable         Arguments                  Description                
#  acpiacadapter                     ACPI ac adapter state.                   
#  acpifan                           ACPI fan state                           
#  acpitemp                          ACPI temperature.                        
#  adt746xcpu                        CPU temperature from therm_adt746x       
#  adt746xfan                        Fan speed from therm_adt746x             
#  battery           (num)           Remaining capasity in ACPI or APM        
#                                    battery. ACPI battery number can be      
#                                    given as argument (default is BAT0).     
#  buffers                           Amount of memory buffered                
#  cached                            Amount of memory cached                  
#  color             (color)         Change drawing color to color            
#  cpu                               CPU usage in percents                    
#  cpubar            (height)        Bar that shows CPU usage, height is      
#                                    bar's height in pixels                   
#  downspeed         net             Download speed in kilobytes              
#  downspeedf        net             Download speed in kilobytes with one     
#                                    decimal                                  
#  exec              shell command   Executes a shell command and displays    
#                                    the output in torsmo. warning: this      
#                                    takes a lot more resources than other    
#                                    variables. I'd recommend coding wanted   
#                                    behaviour in C and posting a patch :-).  
#  execi             interval, shell Same as exec but with specific interval. 
#                    command         Interval can't be less than              
#                                    update_interval in configuration.        
#  fs_bar            (height), (fs)  Bar that shows how much space is used on 
#                                    a file system. height is the height in   
#                                    pixels. fs is any file on that file      
#                                    system.                                  
#  fs_free           (fs)            Free space on a file system available    
#                                    for users.                               
#  fs_free_perc      (fs)            Free percentage of space on a file       
#                                    system available for users.              
#  fs_size           (fs)            File system size                         
#  fs_used           (fs)            File system used space                   
#  hr                (height)        Horizontal line, height is the height in 
#                                    pixels                                   
#  i2c               (dev), type, n  I2C sensor from sysfs (Linux 2.6). dev   
#                                    may be omitted if you have only one I2C  
#                                    device. type is either in (or vol)       
#                                    meaning voltage, fan meaning fan or temp 
#                                    meaning temperature. n is number of the  
#                                    sensor. See /sys/bus/i2c/devices/ on     
#                                    your local computer.                     
#  kernel                            Kernel version                           
#  loadavg           (1), (2), (3)   System load average, 1 is for past 1     
#                                    minute, 2 for past 5 minutes and 3 for   
#                                    past 15 minutes.                         
#  machine                           Machine, i686 for example                
#  mails                             Mail count in mail spool. You can use    
#                                    program like fetchmail to get mails from 
#                                    some server using your favourite         
#                                    protocol. See also new_mails.            
#  mem                               Amount of memory in use                  
#  membar            (height)        Bar that shows amount of memory in use   
#  memmax                            Total amount of memory                   
#  memperc                           Percentage of memory in use              
#  new_mails                         Unread mail count in mail spool.         
#  nodename                          Hostname                                 
#  outlinecolor      (color)         Change outline color                     
#  pre_exec          shell command   Executes a shell command one time before 
#                                    torsmo displays anything and puts output 
#                                    as text.                                 
#  processes                         Total processes (sleeping and running)   
#  running_processes                 Running processes (not sleeping),        
#                                    requires Linux 2.6                       
#  shadecolor        (color)         Change shading color                     
#  stippled_hr       (space),        Stippled (dashed) horizontal line        
#                    (height)        
#  swapbar           (height)        Bar that shows amount of swap in use     
#  swap                              Amount of swap in use                    
#  swapmax                           Total amount of swap                     
#  swapperc                          Percentage of swap in use                
#  sysname                           System name, Linux for example           
#  time              (format)        Local time, see man strftime to get more 
#                                    information about format                 
#  totaldown         net             Total download, overflows at 4 GB on     
#                                    Linux with 32-bit arch and there doesn't 
#                                    seem to be a way to know how many times  
#                                    it has already done that before torsmo   
#                                    has started.                             
#  totalup           net             Total upload, this one too, may overflow 
#  updates                           Number of updates (for debugging)        
#  upspeed           net             Upload speed in kilobytes                
#  upspeedf          net             Upload speed in kilobytes with one       
#                                    decimal                                  
#  uptime                            Uptime                                   
#  uptime_short                      Uptime in a shorter format               

#${execi 120 fortune -s | fold -w50}

# blue color ${color 246eb5}

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen

TEXT
${font marvosym:size=14}U${font} ${goto 70}$uptime				${goto 140}${font marvosym:size=12}j${font} $memperc%  ${mem}
CPU Temp: ${color orange}${acpitempf}°F${color}					${goto 140}${membar 5,120}
${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=12}x${font} ${cpu cpu1}% ${goto 70}${freq_g} GHz	${goto 140}${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=12}t${font} ${cpu cpu2}% ${goto 210}${freq_g} GHz
${cpubar cpu1 5,120}								${goto 140}${cpubar cpu2 5,120}
```

**rhythmbox config**
```
# set to yes if you want Conky to be forked in the background
background yes

cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 2

out_to_console no

# X font when Xft is disabled, you can pick one with program xfontsel
#font 7x12
#font 6x10
#font 7x13
#font 8x13
#font 7x12
#font *mintsmild.se*
#font -*-*-*-*-*-*-34-*-*-*-*-*-*-*
#font -artwiz-snap-normal-r-normal-*-*-100-*-*-p-*-iso8859-1

# Use Xft?
use_xft yes

# Xft font when Xft is enabled
#xftfont Terminus:size=9
xftfont zekton:size=9

# Text alpha when using Xft
xftalpha 1

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# mail spool
mail_spool $MAIL

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 1

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
own_window_type override

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 200 5
maximum_width 400

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw outlines?
draw_outline no

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders no

# border margins
border_margin 4

# border width
border_width 10

# Default colors and also border colors
default_color white
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color black

# colours
color1 white
# light blue
color2 6892C6
# orange
color3 E77320
# green
color4 78BF39
# red
color5 CC0000

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
#alignment top_left
alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right

# Gap between borders of screen and text
gap_x 10
gap_y 40

# Add spaces to keep things from moving about?  This only affects certain objects.
use_spacer none

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase no

# none, xmms, bmp, audacious, infopipe (default is none)


# boinc (seti) dir
# seti_dir /opt/seti

#	*** EXAILE FORMAT SETTINGS ***
#	${execi 10 exaile}
#		make a call to exaile
#
#	*** PARAMETERS ***
#	--get-title           Print the title of current track
#	--get-album           Print the album of current track
#	--get-artist          Print the artist of current track
#	--get-length          Print the length of current track
#	--current-position    Print the position inside the current track as a percentage
#	--start-minimized     Start Exaile minimized to tray, if possible

#	*** RHYTHMBOX FORMAT SETTINGS ***
#
#	${rhythmbox-client --print-playing}
#              Print the title and artist of the playing song
#
#	${rhythmbox-client --print-playing-format}
#              Print formatted details of the song
#
#	*** PARAMETERS ***
#
#       %at    Album title
#       %aT    Album title in lowercase
#       %aa    Album artist
#       %aA    Album artist in lowercase
#       %ay    Release year of album
#       %an    Album disc number
#       %aN    Album disc number with leading zero
#       %ag    Album genre
#       %aG    Album genre in lowercase
#       %tt    Track title
#       %tT    Track title in lowercase
#       %ta    Track artist
#       %tA    Track artist in lowercase
#       %tn    Track number
#       %tN    Track number with leading zero
#       %td    Track duration
#       %te    Elapsed time of track
#
#       Variables can be combined using quotes. For example "%tn %aa %tt", will
#       print the track number followed by the artist  and  the  title  of  the
#       track.

#rhythmbox
#${color1}${if_running rhythmbox}Artist: ${color}$alignr${exec rhythmbox-client --print-playing-format %ta --no-start}
#${voffset 3}${color1}Title: ${color}$alignr${exec  rhythmbox-client --print-playing-format %tt --no-start}
#${voffset 3}${color1}Album: ${color}$alignr${exec rhythmbox-client --print-playing-format %at --no-start}${font}
#${else}Rhythmbox Closed ${endif} ${color1}${hr 2}$color

#	*** BANSHEE FORMAT SETTINGS ***
#
#	Player Engine Query Options
#
#	  --query-current-state      Current player state
#	  --query-last-state         Last player state
#	  --query-can-pause          Query whether the player can be paused
#	  --query-can-seek           Query whether the player can seek
#	  --query-volume             Player volume
#	  --query-position           Player position in currently playing track
#
#	Playing Track Metadata Query Options
#
#	  --query-uri                URI
#	  --query-artist             Artist Name
#	  --query-album              Album Title
#	  --query-title              Track Title
#	  --query-duration           Duration
#	  --query-track-number       Track Number
#	  --query-track-count        Track Count
#	  --query-disc               Disc Number
#	  --query-year               Year
#	  --query-rating             Rating
#
#	User Interface Options
#
#	  --show|--present           Present the user interface on the active workspace
#	  --hide                     Hide the user interface
#	  --no-present               Do not present the user interface, regardless of any other options
#
#	Artist: $alignr${exec banshee --query-artist --hide-field}
#	Title: ${color}$alignr${exec banshee --query-title --hide-field}
#	Album: ${color}$alignr${exec banshee --query-album --hide-field}

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen

TEXT
${execp conkyRhythmbox --template=/home/clockwork/.conkyscripts/conkyRhythmbox.template}
```
```
${color1}Artist: $alignr${color1}[--datatype=AR]
${color1}Title: $alignr${color1}[--datatype=TI]
${color1}Album: $alignr${color1}[--datatype=AL]
${hr 2}
```

using the cofig for this script from [kaivalagi]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=928168")


**deluge script**
```
# conky configuration
# edited by kaivalagi

# set to yes if you want Conky to be forked in the background
background yes

# Use Xft?
use_xft yes

# Xft font when Xft is enabled
xftfont Terminus:size=10

# Text alpha when using Xft
xftalpha 1

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 30

# This is the number of times Conky will update before quitting.
# Set to zero to run forever.
total_run_times 0

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
own_window no

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 300 5
maximum_width 300

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw outlines?
draw_outline no

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 0

# border margins
border_margin 0

# border width
border_width 0

# Default colors and also border colors
default_color white
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color white

# own window options
own_window		yes
own_window_transparent	yes
own_window_type		override
own_window_hints	undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
alignment top_left
#alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right

# Gap between borders of screen and text
# same thing as passing -x at command line
gap_x 10
gap_y 40

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase no

# number of cpu samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
cpu_avg_samples 2

# number of net samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
net_avg_samples 2

# Force UTF8? note that UTF8 support required XFT
override_utf8_locale no

# Add spaces to keep things from moving about?  This only affects certain objects.
use_spacer none

# colors
color1 white
# light blue
color2 6892C6
# orange
color3 E77320
# green
color4 78BF39
# red
color5 CC0000

# variable is given either in format $variable or in ${variable}. Latter
# allows characters right after the variable and must be used in network
# stuff because of an argument

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen

#${if_running deluge}
#${else}${font Terminus:style=Bold:size=13}   Closed${font}${endif}

TEXT
${color4}${font Terminus:style=Bold:size=16}@ ${font Terminus:style=Bold:size=13}Deluge${font}
${voffset 5}${color1}${font}${exec conkyDeluge} 
```
also written by [kaivalagi]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=946664")

### Post by steveydoteu on 2008-10-21
**OS**

Intrepid 8.10 - GNOME 2.24.0

**GTK (Custom)**

*Controls:* Inverted
*Window Border:* Outline Winter
*Icons:* GNOME-Brave

For the controls and the border you will need to install the package **metacity-themes**. The icons are part of a set called **GNOME-colors** ([http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/GNOME-colors?content=82562](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/GNOME-colors?content=82562)). Additional icons are also from this same set.

**Panels**

Both use a background image.

**Wallpaper**

Screenshot from my Halo 3 shares. Scaled. Background color **#222**.

**Conky**

Conky is all drawn on the desktop, currently running four instances initiated via a small script run at startup.

*conkyhoststat* - top right, displays host, kernel, processes (processes running), uptime, cpu frequency*, load averages, network up/down

*only displays one core of two, as both are always the same

Stuck on the bottom of this at present through laziness is the time and date in calendar form, current day highlighted.

*conkyfilesys* - bottom right, displays the usage of various partitions. used / total space.

*conkyrok* - bottom center, displays information about currently playing track and also my collection from amarok (when I get around to adding to it at least!). All wrapped in an $if statement to only display if amarok is running.

*conkyweather* - bottom left, current conditions, four days ahead basic forecast.

I can post the files and such if people desire.

In the second screenshot running applications are Firefox, Amarok in the tray, and a terminal session.

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2008-10-21
> **SomeGuyDude said:**
> How'd you tweak Opera's speed dial like that??

in .opera/speeddial.ini, just do...

[Size]
Rows=3
Columns=5

...or, whatever numbers you want. i've had at least as many as 18 at a time. the only drawback appears to not being able to do *ctrl+dbl.#*.

### Post by crimesaucer on 2008-10-22
> **eightmillion said:**
> crimesaucer, how do you make the xfce panel transparent?

I used this patch on the xfce4-panel: [http://www.loculus.nl/xfce/files/panel-cairo.patch](http://www.loculus.nl/xfce/files/panel-cairo.patch)


from this page: [http://blog.xfce.org/?p=177](http://blog.xfce.org/?p=177)


It works on both xfce4 w/ compositing, and compiz-fusion. Some panel plugins don't work good (the system tray), and others are just ugly with a gray background (the pager). 


I also use the compiz-fusion "blur" effect to make the panel match my emerald theme.

---

from this page: [http://blog.xfce.org/?p=177](http://blog.xfce.org/?p=177)


It works on both xfce4 w/ compositing, and compiz-fusion. Some panel plugins don't work good (the system tray), and others are just ugly with a gray background (the pager). 


I also use the compiz-fusion "blur" effect to make the panel match my emerald theme.

All patches succeeded in patching, and the xfce4-panel was compiled with no errors..... when I installed it, my panel turned transparent immediately..... all I had to do was remove my plugins that had gray backgrounds. (clock, pager)

### Post by OutOfReach on 2008-10-22
> **SomeGuyDude said:**
> Do you know any way to map Sonata to media hotkeys? GMPC has that feature but I like Sonata far better, and that's making a big headache for me.

I don't map my media keys to Sonata, but instead to mpc.
I created an .Xmodmap file in my home folder and mapped my keys in there for example here's mine:
```

keycode 160 = XF86AudioMute
keycode 174 = XF86AudioLowerVolume
keycode 176 = XF86AudioRaiseVolume
keycode 162 = XF86AudioPause
keycode 144 = XF86AudioPrev
keycode 153 = XF86AudioNext
keycode 232 = XF86AudioStop
``` I did this because it didn't automatically recognize my media keys.
I use openbox, but I don't use rc.xml to bind my keys (but you can bind them in there, but I prefer xbindkeys) I use xbindkeys (might have to install that). I created a .xbindkeys in my home folder and the section that binds to mpc is:
```
"mpc toggle"
    m:0x0 + c:162
    XF86AudioPause
```

Of course there are other bindings, for example "mpc stop" "mpc next".

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-10-23

I changed the color scheme a little bit, moving away from browns and more to grays. 

My icon theme is Snowish.  I had Hydroxygen installed, which is meant for use in GNOME, but that theme had too many icons missing for it to be usable in KDE.

I'm starting to get really disappointed with KDE's selection of icon themes.  Unless there is some website other than KDE-look that has a bunch of them that I don't know about.

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-10-23
> **unoodles said:**
> VERY NICE!! How did you get the entire web page to invert? Whenever I try to invert page using Firefox Preferences, the images do not invert.

First, I installed the Firefox addon called Stylish, which you can get here:
[https://addons.mozilla.org/firefox/addon/2108](https://addons.mozilla.org/firefox/addon/2108)

Next, I installed the Dark Gray Google Stylish code, which you can get here:
[http://userstyles.org/styles/6689](http://userstyles.org/styles/6689)

[B]Conky: use_spacer should have an argument of left, right, or none.  'yes' seems to be some form of 'true', so defaulting to right.
Conky: statfs '/media/data': No such file or directory
Conky: desktop window (100008b) is subwindow of root window (64)
Conky: drawing to desktop window
Conky: drawing to double buffer
Conky: statfs '/media/data': No such file or directory[/B]

I really don't know. I would suggest you, anyway, to change the paths of the lines of that Conky file referring to drive paths. Such as /media/data, etc. Adapt them to the drives or folders you want to monitor.

Then I would also ask you if by any chance you are using Conky under GNOME. There are certain specifics about which window type one should choose on the .conkyrc file, in order not to interfere with Nautilus, which draws the desktop. Usually you would need to change 'own_window no' to 'yes'. As for the 'own_window_type' option, I'm a bit clueless, because I didn't have icons on my GNOME desktop (I almost never like icons on my desktops, except for docks/panels, etc.) when I used it. But try to set that to 'normal' or something. See what happens.

_____________________________________________________________

I think I forgot to say the essential on my previous message... That was my first desktop on Intrepid. The Release Candidate is out already, so I upgraded, as planned. Everything seems fine, until now. I just can't use the file browser plugin on Gedit, or it will hit 100% of CPU usage for some long minutes, until I kill it.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-10-25
Slowly getting to grips with the changes in Xfce4.6. Weird how manually defining icon sizes in your gtkrc doesn't work anymore. There's *some* ability to control toolbar icon-size via xfconf and this new method appears to have solved the issue in Firefox where setting icons to be scalable and smaller than the default resulted in Firefox trying to upscale them w/o antialiasing.

[url=http://img162.imageshack.us/img162/457/newmenuspi4.jpg][img]http://img260.imageshack.us/img260/9084/newmenussmp7.jpg[/img]
http://img162.imageshack.us/img162/457/newmenuspi4.jpg[/url]
Those are the default menu layouts, BTW. You can go back to the old window list w/o submenus but there doesn't appear to be a way to edit the root menu yet.

Still can't figure out how to force the xfdesktop menus to adopt custom icon sizing, though. Nor does it appear that you're allowed to use, "kiosk mode" (right-click desktop opens up root menu, not desktop menu) without turning off desktop icons.

[url=http://img373.imageshack.us/img373/7480/newconfrb2.jpg][img]http://img373.imageshack.us/img373/7971/newconfsqg2.jpg[/img]
http://img373.imageshack.us/img373/7480/newconfrb2.jpg[/url]
Would be cool if the xfconf editor eventually included support for gconf editing. Save having to install separate tools as it's basically inevitable that you're going to have GTK+ apps which use gconf.

Xfconf daemon also appears to misbehave a bit at the moment. Cursor theme isn't sticking. Display settings offer a pretty interface which does nothing. Obviously, it's only a beta and for the most part, I'm enjoying it, though.

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-10-25
Decided to do some major tweaks to my Kubuntu desktop.

First I ripped the black folder icons and the mimetype icons from Hydroxygen and surgically inserted them into the Breathless icon theme for KDE.

Next, I changed my Emerald theme to better imitate the original Dust Metacity.

I decided to take the Dust color scheme to a new level by replacing the grey portions of the theme with the dark grey used by the rest of the theme.  I also changed the selected color from the light brown-grey to a yellow-orange color.  I reflected that color change in my Emerald theme, my Kicker, and the Knewsticker applet at the top of my screen.

Next, I changed my fonts from Calibri Bold 9 to Corbel 9.

Finally, I replaced the icons in my Cairo-Dock with better custom-made ones.
