### Post by elmer_42 on 2008-10-25
> **OutOfReach said:**
> Nice, mind sharing your Tint2 config?
Here you go, I hope it helps!
```
#---------------------------------------------
# TINT CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_mode = single_desktop
panel_monitor = 1
panel_position = bottom center
panel_size = 1440 25
panel_margin = 0 0
panel_padding = 2 0
font_shadow = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
panel_rounded = 0
panel_border_width = 0
panel_background_color = #303030 100
panel_border_color = #ffffff 18

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 155
task_margin = 1
task_padding = 1
task_icon_size = 16
task_font = dejavu-sans book 8
task_font_color = #bebebe 25
task_active_font_color = #bebebe 100

#---------------------------------------------
# TASK BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
task_rounded = 0
task_background_color = #ffffff 0
task_active_background_color = #000000 10
task_border_width = 0
task_border_color = #ffffff 0
task_active_border_color = #bebebe 3

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
time1_format = %a %b %d %H:%M  
time1_font = dejavu-sans book 8
#time2_format = %a %b %d
#time2_font = sans 6
clock_font_color = #bebebe 25

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = close
mouse_right = none
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify
```

### Post by Mazza558 on 2008-10-26
I have a new aim: a Desktop which "just works". Nothing more than what is needed in terms of buttons/the interface. I've been modding a murrine GTK theme to make it completely functional and still looking very nice. I'm using a combination of 2 emerald themes which looks nice and is easy to use. ### Post by narf41 on 2008-10-26
reworked my desk
-gtk:my own (new features are workarounds for firefox and openoffice to get bold text in menubar/menus in these applications too - look at the second screenshot...okok in openoffice all ui-text is bold :D )
-killed the scrollbars from firefox
-emerald:based on flatwillow with little changes (shadows, title...)
-icons: hydroxygen
-wall:something from deviantart, i killed the color :)

### Post by MaxIBoy on 2008-10-26
> **DJ_Peng said:**
> You may want to check out Gnome Do, fballem. That's let me pull a bunch of launchers off my desktop and my frequently used apps are just a couple (or so) of keys away.

I prefer to put things like that on a panel, so it's only one key away. Furthermore, the edge of the screen is the best possible place for a button, because the effective size of the target is bigger. *really* commonly used stuff should go in the corners (which is why I dislike the default placement of the recycle bin and "show desktop" buttons.)

---

### Post by raul_ on 2008-10-26
> **cookieofdoom said:**
> I like it. Obviously KDE4... Is that Arch or Ubuntu? and what is the plasmoid on the left? Kopete integration to plasma? *looking very interested*

:) it's Arch.

The kopete plasmoid is actually a lancelot component. Lancelot is a substitute for kde's default menu, and when you install it, you get to use each of its separate components as plasmoids (contacts, mail, recently used documents, favorites, etc)

I'm using KDEmod but it's based on 4.1.2. It's pretty stable for me, but I would wait till *at least the hard freeze on 4.2 for some polishing (that's happening november 17th). I'm hoping kdemod devs follow that update.

Suspend doesn't work for me, but that's my laptops fault.

You may have noticed that I don't have any menu at all. That's because klauncher is pretty powerful now, and I can just alt+f2 and type, for example, "shutdown" :cool:

### Post by Boaslad on 2008-10-26
This is what I am currently using. It's simple, but its functional, and VERY relaxing.
It uses a "Tactile" theme and "Gion" icons
The marbling effect on the unfocused window is caused by a combined use of the "Reflection" and "Trailfocus" tools in Compiz.
This also causes the bright edges around all the windows and tool bars.
The wallpaper is "Mysterium.jpg"

### Post by ad_267 on 2008-10-29
That was explained in this thread a while back. I think basically there's a "profile" that needs to be changed to "style" somewhere in the gtkrc for people using the Murrine engine in Intrepid.

```

$ aptitude show gtk2-engines-murrine
Package: gtk2-engines-murrine
State: installed
Automatically installed: no
Version: 0.60.1
Priority: optional
Section: x11
Maintainer: Ubuntu MOTU Developers <ubuntu-motu@lists.ubuntu.com>

```

---

### Post by perfectska04@hotmail.com on 2008-10-29
> **dbbolton said:**
> Thanks.

I don't know either. I just commented it out in my newer themes. I haven't been able to find any documentation on the new engine.

hilight_ratio is deprecated, but highlight_ratio isn't.

Also, you can use a combination of gradient_shades and highlight_ratio to achieve the "style" or "profile" you want, without risking compatibility with the old murrine in intrepid or the new one. I use that method for drawing clearlooks-like scrollbars and progressbars in Shiki-Colors without having to use "profile" or "style" so it works with pretty much any version of Murrine SVN. If you just want regular, glossy, murrine widgets then just skip the profile/style values, it will be used automatically.

---

### Post by elmer_42 on 2008-10-29
> **SomeGuyDude said:**
> Bwahahha. Finally got a GTK theme that works perfectly. Minor conky update, but that's it. Basically I found the MiniWhite theme on Gnome-Look and it just fit beautifully with the new black/white motif.
I see you have Alsa Mixer in your menu. If I remember correctly, that is an ncurses (terminal) app. What command do you use to run it?

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-10-29
> **Oldster said:**
> I have a question for the experts. The Elegant Brit theme is informing me that the correct gtk engine is not installed. I looked through the theme's configuration files and didn't really find an answer.

How does one determine the correct gtk engine for a theme?

You need the pixmap and/or pixbuf engines. You can tell by opening up a theme's gtkrc file and looking for *engine "pixmap"* in the file.

---

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2008-10-29

Finally got my Xfce 4.4 to come to its senses. Deleted my top panel. Trying out a different concept on the bottom panel. ### Post by dbbolton on 2008-10-30
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> FTR, I compiled the latest Murrine SVN this morning and I had still had to change any instance of, "profile", to, "style" and there was something else causing it to fail on line 405 or 406 which I had to change (think it was @selected_bg_color).

From my understanding, "profile" is supposed to replace "style". But I really have no idea.

As for lines 405-6:

```

    bg[NORMAL]        = "#222222"
    bg[PRELIGHT]     = @selected_bg_color

```

They look syntactically sound to me.

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2008-10-30
> **elmer_42 said:**
> Chucky, I thank you profusely for this. This may change the way I use the Openbox menu.

my pleasure, my friend. i've used that a lot. it also works if you use a file manager like thunar. when you right-click on a text file, for example, and you wish you could open it in nano/vim, you can use *terminal -e nano/vim* in the command line option and check the "use this always" (or, whatever it says) option. it also works with music files, with something like *terminal -e cplay*. ("*terminal*" can be whichever terminal you wish, xterm, urxvt, whatever...)

another useful trick, speaking of the openbox menu, is for panels. i will make a new menu entry and call it pypanel. for one menu entry i will have 'on' with the command *pypanel* and another entry labeled 'off', with the command *killall pypanel*. it's a little blunt, but effective.

good times!

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-10-30

    bg[NORMAL]        = "#222222"
    bg[PRELIGHT]     = @selected_bg_color

```

They look syntactically sound to me.
That's right. Wouldn't work until I replaced @selected_bg_color with it's equivalent hex. I couldn't figure out why it was being so picky, either.

Conkyrc plz. That or the section which shows how you got the graph titles like that.

---

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2008-10-31
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Conkyrc plz. That or the section which shows how you got the graph titles like that.

It's heavy abuse of the offset tags. Here you go. If you're doing it on a vertical conky it's a LOT easier because don't have to keep "un-offsetting" it. 

```
${color 000000}${voffset 1}${membar 6,100}${offset -100}${voffset -1}${color white}Mem${color 000000}${offset 80}${color}  | ${voffset 1}${color 000000}${fs_bar 6,100 /home}${offset -100}${color white}${voffset -1}Home${color 000000}${offset 80}${color} | ${voffset 1}${color 000000}${fs_bar 6,100 /}${offset -100}${voffset -1}${color white}Root${color 000000}${offset 80} ${color}
```

---

### Post by tjwoosta on 2008-10-31
> That's amazing...I looove the last one how did you do that?

thanks

do what?  compiz?

icon theme: gorilla

gtk theme: clearlooks (modified colors, the dark color is #272727)

emerald theme: Red-Alice (modified colors, change contrast all the way up for titlebar, use #272727 and #FFFFFF, shadow_color: Black, play around with the shadow radius and offsets and opacity untill it looks right, change anything that was red to #272727)

GNOME Panel Background: attached 

Skydome: I used the Intergalactic Theme's Skydome but i desaturated it with gimp to make it black and white
link[http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Intergalactic%3A+Compiz+Edition?content=78809]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Intergalactic%3A+Compiz+Edition?content=78809")

wallpaper:[http://www.filefactory.com/file/f77c0c/n/Green_Wallpaper_openSUSE_tar_gz]("http://www.filefactory.com/file/f77c0c/n/Green_Wallpaper_openSUSE_tar_gz")
(that link is actually free despite the way it looks, the free link is down towards the bottom of the page)
